In [2]:
import csv, codecs, re,xml.etree.ElementTree
from time import sleep
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import numpy as np

During mylastsemester of DCC, I had to maintain a wordpress blog. After doingmy posts I never looked back at it untilI got an email asking to moderate the comments. On a whim I decided to check back in to find over 2800 comments made by spam bots. Even while I'm writing this dozens are being added. So I decided to analyze them. Why? I'm messed up in the head and bored.

In [3]:
word_dict = {}
ip_dict = {}
author_dict = {}
website_dict = {}
email_dict = {}
hour_dict = {}
time_dict = {}
num_mistakes_dict = {}
error_dict = {}

with codecs.open('data/spam_data.csv','r',encoding="utf-8") as spam_data:
    reader = csv.DictReader(spam_data)
    for row in reader:
        # Getting word count
        comment = row['Comment']
        
        for word in comment.split():
            word = re.sub("[\?\.,\“!\"\”\(\)]","",word)
            #print(word)
            if word in word_dict:
                word_dict[word] += 1
            else:
                word_dict[word] = 1
    
    
        # Getting IP count
        ip = row['IP Address']
        if ip in ip_dict:
            ip_dict[ip] += 1
        else:
            ip_dict[ip] = 1
        # Getting author count
        author = row['Author']
        if author in author_dict:
            author_dict[author] += 1
        else:
            author_dict[author] = 1
        # Getting website count
        website = row['Website']
        if website in website_dict:
            website_dict[website] += 1
        else:
            website_dict[website] = 1
        # Getting email count
        email = row['Email']
        if email in email_dict:
            email_dict[email] += 1
        else:
            email_dict[email] = 1

        # Getting hour frequency
        hour = re.sub(":[\d]{2}","",row['Submit Time'])

        hour_number = re.match("[\d]+",hour).group(0)
        if "pm" in hour:
            hour = str((int(hour_number)+12)%24)+":00"
        else:
            hour = str((int(hour_number))%24)+":00" 
        if len(hour) < 5:
            hour = "0"+hour
            
        if hour in hour_dict:
            hour_dict[hour] += 1
        else:
            hour_dict[hour] = 1
            
        #Getting time frequency by converting to military time
        time = re.match("([\d]+):([\d]{2})",row['Submit Time'])
        #print(time.groups())
        time_string = ""
        
        if "pm" in row['Submit Time']:
            time_string = str((int(time.groups()[0])+12)%24)+":"+str(time.groups()[1])
        else:
            time_string = str(int(time.groups()[0]))+":"+str(time.groups()[1])
        time_check = re.match("([\d]+):([\d]{2})",time_string)
        if len(time_check.groups()[0]) < 2:
            time_string = "0"+time_string
        if time_string in time_dict:
            time_dict[time_string] += 1
        else:
            time_dict[time_string] = 1
        
        # Grammar checking - number of errors
        parse_tree = xml.etree.ElementTree.fromstring(row['Grammar Check'])
        num_mistakes_dict[row['Comment Number']] = [len(parse_tree),row['Comment']]
        error_dict[row['Comment Number']] = parse_tree

Now, let's see what are the most common words used by these commentors.

In [23]:
words_sorted = reversed(sorted(word_dict.items(), key=lambda x: x[1]))
for (word,count) in words_sorted:
    print(word,"-",count)

So there are many of the usually boring repeated words: "I", "the", "a", etc. As with almost anytext, these dominate the top of words used. However further down there are moreinteresting words that crop up: "site", "web", "blog", and "website." Most of these comments wanted to heap comments upon my website or blog (post) and/or try toconvince people to visittheir websites and links.

WordPress also stores the IP Adresses of every comment author. Below are listed the addresses.

In [24]:
ips_sorted = reversed(sorted(ip_dict.items(), key=lambda x: x[1]))
for (ip,count) in ips_sorted:
    print(ip,"-",count)

162.144.116.254 - 2749
89.32.181.200 - 86
202.80.213.17 - 20
62.210.80.55 - 3
23.106.27.200 - 3
23.80.140.198 - 1
23.80.140.52 - 1
82.196.9.133 - 1
12.181.44.68 - 1
67.205.159.245 - 1
121.193.143.249 - 1
185.104.217.197 - 1
185.104.219.83 - 1
112.196.25.141 - 1

Wow! This one IP address, "162.144.116.254", seems to be the main source of all this spam! What could it be? Oh ... "dcc.umd.edu." Well either WordPress messed up, other IP Adresses are found by commenting via external means, or the commenters are good at hiding their IP addresses.

I have noclue. Possible ad revenue from clicks/visits? SEO? I have nary a clue.

Nothing seems all that unusual here. That might be because emails aren'thard to fake,they're a simple pattern: randomname + number then add an "@" followed by a well known email provider. It's pretty spread out list and I don't really think there is much to gain because it's too hard to ascertain if these are "real" or "active" emails.

Another area of curiosity is the time allthese comments were submitted.

Now let's see the distribution errors we have.

In [19]:
error_type_dict = {}
for key in error_dict:
    for child in error_dict[key]:
        error_type = child.find('type').text
        if error_type not in error_type_dict:
            error_type_dict[error_type] = 1
        else:
            error_type_dict[error_type] += 1
for key in error_type_dict:
    print(key,"-",error_type_dict[key])

grammar - 3008
spelling - 1396

It seems that the most common type of mistakes are grammatical ones.

Now let's see what are the most misspelled words.

In [19]:
misspelled_words = {}
for key in error_dict:
    for child in error_dict[key]:
        error_type = child.find('type').text
        if error_type == "spelling":
            word = child.find('string').text
            if word not in misspelled_words:
                misspelled_words[word] = 1
            else: 
                misspelled_words[word] += 1
                
wrong_words = reversed(sorted(misspelled_words.items(),key=lambda x:x[1]))
for (word,count) in wrong_words:
    print(word,"-",count)

Well most of these seem to be words that are missing punctuation marks or are slang. This suggests that the people making these spam comments at least know of english words. They may not full understand or wantto use punctuation (this could be some programming hitch since an apostrophe is a single quote used to mark strings). Also they could've included the slang, and kept it informal, in order to mimic non-spam texts made online made by genuine users that employthese words.
